    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText15509144649866887225" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <em>In a land on the brink of peace—watched jealously by a ruthless cult from across the sea and beset by hidden enemies—five extraordinary humans must serve as sword and shield of the Gods.<br /><br />Auraya is one.<br /><br /></em>
</blockquote>Her heroism saved a village from destruction; now Auraya has been named Priestess of the White. The limits of her unique talents must be tested in order to prove her worthy of the honor and grave responsibility awarded to her. But a perilous road lies ahead, fraught with pitfalls that will challenge the newest servant of the gods. An enduring friendship with a Dreamweaver—a member of an ancient outcast sect of sorcerer-healers—could destroy Auraya's future. And her destiny has set her in conflict with a powerful and mysterious, black-clad sorcerer with but a single purpose: the total annihilation of the White. And he is not alone . . .</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41237958" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3935419384208004081">Okay, I give up. I couldn't even finish this one, which is very rare for me--and I had less than a hundred pages to go. I had put it down one night and have not been able to make myself pick it back up again.<br/><br/>I found it to be completely boring, despite the interesting concepts and potential conflicts. This book just <i>drug</i>. Not much action to move it along. Gets bogged down in what seem to be side-stories (they may come together at the end, I'll never know). I liked this authors previous series, so</span>
  <span id="freeText3935419384208004081" style="display:none">Okay, I give up. I couldn't even finish this one, which is very rare for me--and I had less than a hundred pages to go. I had put it down one night and have not been able to make myself pick it back up again.<br /><br />I found it to be completely boring, despite the interesting concepts and potential conflicts. This book just <i>drug</i>. Not much action to move it along. Gets bogged down in what seem to be side-stories (they may come together at the end, I'll never know). I liked this authors previous series, so this was a disappointment.</span>

<div id="review_177903301" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177903301" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5657700-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580342355p2/5657700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177903301?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/5657700-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841495156" href="/book/show/460334.Priestess_of_the_White">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177903301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer810467971070982466">I would have actually given this book 3,5 stars but there's no such scale. <br/>After reading The Black Magician trilogy I expected this one to be better... there was nothing wrong with the style of writing but I wanted something fresh, something new. And here? I'm getting a copy of Canavan's previous novel.<br/>The motive of forbidden romance between Sonea and Akkarin is very similar to the one that Auraya and Leiard struggle with. Despite the fact that they are featureless (most of the characters in thi</span>
  <span id="freeText810467971070982466" style="display:none">I would have actually given this book 3,5 stars but there's no such scale. <br />After reading The Black Magician trilogy I expected this one to be better... there was nothing wrong with the style of writing but I wanted something fresh, something new. And here? I'm getting a copy of Canavan's previous novel.<br />The motive of forbidden romance between Sonea and Akkarin is very similar to the one that Auraya and Leiard struggle with. Despite the fact that they are featureless (most of the characters in this book actually are boring and nothing pushes me towards any of them stronger than the others... with one exception I'm gonna write about later). To be honest the main heroin annoys me. I hope that there won't be much about her in the 2nd volume... 'cause as it's called 'Last of the Wilds' I'm positive there's gonna be much more about Emerahl which is probably the only character that has intrigued me with her personality a bit more.<br />I wonder if the author really couldn't create something more original and different from The Black Magician trilogy. It was a huge success but it doesn't mean that you should follow it in that way Miss Canavan ;) As for now in all your books I've read so far an evil nation without any particular reason (oh, maybe except being purely evil) attacks the innocent one. They possess amazingly powerful magic (which is not known by anyone else) and their sorcerers wreak havoc among unarmed people. Yet they are being defeated by valiant defenders which are suspiciously lucky. Unbelievable, isn't it? The only difference is that in the first trilogy the invader is Sachaka and the victim is Kyralia. Here we've got conflict between Pentadrians and Circlians. Still it was obvious for me from the very beginning that the scales of victory are going to tilt on the side of Circlians... and Auraya will be the saviour.<br />One more thing that irritated me was poor duplication of Sonea in the person of Auraya - the chosen one, the brave, the greatest, loved and admired by everyone. It's not that funny as it was for the first time, especially that Sonea was way better and much more likable than Auraya. Not only that I don't like her but sadly I have to admit that I can't stand her and her fake willingness to be the good White.<br />Maybe my rating would be higher if not the fact that I read The Black Magician trilogy first and was delighted by the plot, completely new way of understanding magic and putting young apprentices into the Magicians' Guild. But I won't give up and gonna finish the whole trilogy, hope it's gonna be worth it ;) </span>
  <a data-text-id="810467971070982466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1677282762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1677282762" />
    <a title="Tommye Turner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30506556-tommye-turner"><img alt="Tommye Turner" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1677282762?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tommye Turner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tommye Turner" href="/user/show/30506556-tommye-turner">Tommye Turner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30506556-tommye-turner?shelf=fantasy-read">fantasy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1677282762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5862907479080160641">SPOILER FREE<br/><br/>This novel is where my love of reading big fantasy books began when I was 11 or 12 years old. I was on holiday on the Isle of Mull and the only thing close to us that was at all interesting (to a kid of that age) was a book shop in Tobermory. I picked this wonderful fantasy novel up there and I've re-read it more than any other book I own. I quickly finished the trilogy within a week. <br/><br/>Despite having read this book so young, I’d suggest reading it yourself before giving it to a child </span>
  <span id="freeText5862907479080160641" style="display:none">SPOILER FREE<br /><br />This novel is where my love of reading big fantasy books began when I was 11 or 12 years old. I was on holiday on the Isle of Mull and the only thing close to us that was at all interesting (to a kid of that age) was a book shop in Tobermory. I picked this wonderful fantasy novel up there and I've re-read it more than any other book I own. I quickly finished the trilogy within a week. <br /><br />Despite having read this book so young, I’d suggest reading it yourself before giving it to a child as it is an adult fantasy book with scenes that you might not be comfortable with your child reading!<br />Auraya is a brilliant character. She’s deeply religious and struggles to fit in with others of the Gods’ chosen five. She quickly dives into the political issues of the world in securing alliances and preparing for possible war. We see her grow so much in this book, from a child in the prologue to a fierce, passionate adult. <br /><br />There are several other POV character in this book who all add a little more to the world that Canavan has created. There are many secrets and hidden mysteries yet to be uncovered and it’s exciting to follow as the characters work them out or reveal them to us when they are ready. <br /><br />This is a great first book of the trilogy. Many negative reviews talk about Canavan’s writing style. I found it accessible and to the point. There is nothing flowery to it, but it’s solid and I soon found myself lost in the story and the world. <br /><br />Canavan’s work doesn’t get enough praise or attention. I hope more people will pick up these books in the future so they get the attention they deserve. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5862907479080160641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1527827281" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1527827281" />
    <a title="PaperTigerMaddy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5380743-papertigermaddy"><img alt="PaperTigerMaddy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505152729p2/5380743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1527827281?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PaperTigerMaddy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PaperTigerMaddy" href="/user/show/5380743-papertigermaddy">PaperTigerMaddy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5380743-papertigermaddy?shelf=doesn-t-deserve-the-hype">doesn-t-deserve-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5380743-papertigermaddy?shelf=god-awful-writing">god-awful-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5380743-papertigermaddy?shelf=did-this-actually-see-an-editor">did-this-actually-see-an-editor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5380743-papertigermaddy?shelf=black-and-white">black-and-white</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5380743-papertigermaddy?shelf=slow">slow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5380743-papertigermaddy?shelf=plot-what-plot">plot-what-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5380743-papertigermaddy?shelf=worldbuilding-what-worldbuilding">worldbuilding-what-worldbuilding</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5380743-papertigermaddy?shelf=multiple-protagonists">multiple-protagonists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5380743-papertigermaddy?shelf=all-of-the-gingers">all-of-the-gingers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5380743-papertigermaddy?shelf=all-of-the-badass-ladies">all-of-the-badass-ladies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1527827281" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9023639132180541541">Edit: dropped this rating down from 2.5 to a 1 because it's really not worth anyone's time.<br/> Why the heck has this been rated so high? It's crap, especially compared to her excellent debut trilogy! The respect I had for Canavan's writing has largely evaporated. I hope this terrible book was simply a dud, and not that the Black Magician trilogy was a fluke.<br/><br/><br/>Okay, gripe #1. Plants, animals and vehicles are given totally random names despite being albeit identical to things we have in this world. Why</span>
  <span id="freeText9023639132180541541" style="display:none">Edit: dropped this rating down from 2.5 to a 1 because it's really not worth anyone's time.<br /> Why the heck has this been rated so high? It's crap, especially compared to her excellent debut trilogy! The respect I had for Canavan's writing has largely evaporated. I hope this terrible book was simply a dud, and not that the Black Magician trilogy was a fluke.<br /><br /><br />Okay, gripe #1. Plants, animals and vehicles are given totally random names despite being albeit identical to things we have in this world. Why? Who bloody knows. To purposefully confuse the novel? Maybe! When a Reyna is 'a swift flighty animal used for riding' mate you are literally just describing a horse so for the love of god just say HORSE<br /><br />This however is the only complex thing about the novel, which is otherwise let down by its sheer simplicity. The writing tells, not shows, to the point where it reads awkwardly and childishly. Dialogue is affected and stupid. Witness 16 year old Auraya on page 9: <br /><br />'Even I, living in this tiny village, know of the famous Dunwayan Fire-Warrior Clan'. <br /><br />Oh god. At this point I was already groaning. Entire paragraphs are wasted with people repeating each other's formal titles and greetings. It's all 'Welcome, Auraya of the White' this and 'She made the sign of the circle' that.<br /><br /><br />Excessive exposition from characters' internal monologues when they ponder over their emotions is also so overused it's stupid. Witness pages 42-44:<br /><br />'Her father's letters were, by necessity, short. She felt a wary relief after she read more of them. We were careful, she thought. (Ok, point established.) We didn't say exactly what we were doing. (Yes, we got that.) Except for the first letter I sent, in which I had to make it plain what I wanted Father to do. (CLEARLY!?) Hopefully he burned that one. She sighed and shook her head. No matter how careful she and her father had been, the gods must know what they had done. They could see into the minds of all. Yet they still chose me, she thought. Of all the high priestesses, they chose someone who had broken the law and used a Dreamweaver's services. (We GET it. My god. Cut forward a page). I was so sure this would stand against me being chosen (are you STILL talking about this?!) I wanted so much to be part of the White....but the gods still chose me. What am I to make of that? (One paragraph later) Why would the gods do that? (Gahhh! Kill me!) (Okay screw this I'm not typing out the next 1.5 pages, suffice it to say IT IS ALL THE SAME)<br /><br /><br />*inhales deeply* yes calm<br /><br /><br />This is a shame, as it is character interaction and internal dialogue which is a key strength of the Black Magician trilogy. Worse, this (lack of) style here washes away much of the benefit gained by Canavan's core strength - her ability to create a large cast of relatable, distinct and likeable characters.<br /><br /><br /><br />While the occasional stab is made at scenery description, in general very little world building has gone here, and we are left with a minimal sense of place and atmosphere. An entire continent! With no sense of place! Battle scenes are reduced to one liners such as 'She blasted him with magic'. Ooooh! Description stretches to things like 'There was a mountain range.' K thanks Trudi das cool I feel totally swept away. Not. And no, stupid animal names do not a substitute make. <br /><br /><br /><br />We are supposed to blindly accept that the Pentadrians are evil, with literally zero realistic motive provided for their invasion. Mainly, because they wear black, carry pentacles (bwahahaha!) they are CLEARLY evil, right? Why are they evil, you ask? Because they just ARE BWAHAHAHAHA!!! Now stop asking stupid questions.<br /><br /><br />Also, did anyone else find it weird that the only explicitly PoC characters (apart from the creepy fish people) were the evil ones? Seriously? What is this, Tolkien? <br /><br /><br />Similarly, the Circlian gods are never developed past a blind acceptance that they are all mighty and all-benevolent, despite occasional hints that this might not be the case. The White are also happy skippy all benevolent all frolicking servant/king/priests, with no apparent flaws in their governance or self interest to make them more believable. They don't even really seem to dislike Dreamweaver's all that much! Apart from the 'truly regrettable' death of Mirar (Agh the terrible guilt upon Juran's unstained conscience! It's so hard being flawless!) everything they do is...utopian. Which is totes ridic.<br /><br />There is no suggestion that (as I suspect-potential spoiler) the Pentadrians are exactly like the Circlians, and the war is all an evil ploy of two evil groups of gods. Further development on these any of these fronts would have made for a far stronger novel. Instead it is super one sided and crap. <br /><br /><br />What is left is a one road plot with no depth. And as a result in part of this lack of plot development, Canavan is forced to fish around for alternative, random, one-shot narrative voices (OTHER than her main characters!) in order to give the story depth. While it isn't unusual for writers to have one major POV and then a series of random minor one-shot POVs (Horowitz springs to mind), it IS weird to have a cast of major POVs (five if you count Auraya, Leiard, Danjin and Tryss) and STILL need more! This is messy, and a sign of poor writing in my opinion. If your main characters cannot give the story enough colour, you have a problem. <br /><br /><br />Now as for the actual characters. I wanted to like Auraya, but her chapters are let down by the overly affected exposition I've already discussed. She's also extremely bland, as other reviewed have mentioned. Same for Leiard. Though I got their attraction, it turned into love out of nowhere. And then became totally meh. Romantic love scenes are censored, but perfunctory brothel sex is not. Why!? Damnit WHY!!?!<br /><br /><br />Let's be real: Tryss' entire story line is extraneous to the plot, not to mention the most boring and childlike of the lot. It should have been cut, or a better way found to incorporate the Siyee. I never really got over the line 'He meant to fly on, but found himself circling, fascinated by the small dark hollow between her breasts.' YE GODS. The only POV I truly enjoyed was Emerahl's adventures in the brothel, though ironically this is also pointless up until the final chapter. Now, a novel about HER I would like to read. But with more sex.<br /><br /><br />All in all, a massive let down. Come on Canavan, we know you can do better than this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9023639132180541541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16984700632326146217">This is a review for ALL of the books, ie. the whole series. <br/><br/>I started the book about 5 or 6 Months before I finished it, but never got past the first fifty pages. I had liked the Black Magician Trilogy, but I thought I didn't like the theme too much in this book. <br/>Yet, in the end, I think I totally prefer this series to the other!<br/><br/>There were many positive points in the series.   <span id="freeText16984700632326146217" style="display:none">This is a review for ALL of the books, ie. the whole series. <br /><br />I started the book about 5 or 6 Months before I finished it, but never got past the first fifty pages. I had liked the Black Magician Trilogy, but I thought I didn't like the theme too much in this book. <br />Yet, in the end, I think I totally prefer this series to the other!<br /><br />There were many positive points in the series. It was more complex and the plot and the world seemed very well deverloped. It had more mature themes, which are definitely not too suited for Teenagers (It says on the website that she wanted a more "Sex, Drugs and Violence" theme), but the main ones are Religion and Belief. I think the Ideas for the Religions are very interesting and unconventional - but this is only revealed later on. <br /><br />I definitely think that one of Trudi Canavan's Strength lies in the last books. As the series goes on, it develops more excitement and friction. Thus, the last book is definitely the best. <br /><br />I reread this trilogy afterwards and It confirmed to me what I have thought once again. The Black Magician trilogy is not half as entertaining or well made - to me. I'm in love with this world much more than I am with Kyralia, i can relate much better to the Characters and the flaws in the plot can be overlooked.<br />This is not the common opinion, I know, but I stick to it. These books are Trudi Canavan's best. </span>

<div id="review_393298426" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/393298426" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2664101-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298377267p2/2664101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/393298426?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/2664101-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841495156" href="/book/show/460334.Priestess_of_the_White">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2664101-becky?shelf=read-for-myself">read-for-myself</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2664101-becky?shelf=adult-fantasy">adult-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer393298426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17965708981223716110">Priestess of the White is the first novel in Trudi Canavan’s Age of Five series.<br/><br/><br/>Set in a fantastical world where Gods have chosen representatives to do their bidding in the world, this novel mixes magic and religion. The leaders of Hania are the White – five powerful sorcerers who are guided by their Gods. Auraya is the youngest of the White and the novel begins with her joining the Priesthood and her commitment to devote her life to the will of the Gods.<br/><br/><br/>It is the Gods’ will that all of Northern</span>
  <span id="freeText17965708981223716110" style="display:none">Priestess of the White is the first novel in Trudi Canavan’s Age of Five series.<br /><br /><br />Set in a fantastical world where Gods have chosen representatives to do their bidding in the world, this novel mixes magic and religion. The leaders of Hania are the White – five powerful sorcerers who are guided by their Gods. Auraya is the youngest of the White and the novel begins with her joining the Priesthood and her commitment to devote her life to the will of the Gods.<br /><br /><br />It is the Gods’ will that all of Northern Ithania be united and at peace. Auraya is a problem solver by nature, she is patient and caring. She had a childhood friendship from a Dreamweaver and this makes her more open-minded and accepting of their choices. It is this unique vision that makes Auraya a great peace-maker and her role as a servant of the Gods sees her travel to form alliances with other races in Northern Ithania.<br /><br /><br />This is an epic book and I feel the challenge of summarising the complicated history of the Gods’ past is beyond me. Those who do not follow the Gods they are known as Dreamweavers – the White view them as heathens. The leader of the White killed the leader of the Dreamweavers and there is a deep rooted hatred between these peoples. Dreamweavers are healers and pacifists. They were persecuted by followers of the White and were massacred in the past. Auraya hopes to change the dynamic between the White and the Dreamweavers.<br /><br /><br />While the nations of Northern Ithania are debating alliances with the White, in the South the heathen cult known as the Pentadrians (who follow fake Gods) are readying themselves for war.<br /><br /><br />Trudi Canavan’s storytelling leaves me awestruck. There are so many different plots and subplots running through this novel and they all link together in a coherent mesmerising way. The story is told in Canavan’s usual style – a third person roving viewpoint. We still the events of the story from so many different characters and it could be completely overwhelming but Canavan’s writing is so incredibly clear that it isn’t. <br /><br /><br />The themes in this novel are war and loyalty, the idea of devotion and free will, power and sacrifice, strength and weakness. It was fascinating to read about characters who range from fervent in their belief in their Gods to absolute hatred towards the Gods. It made me feel impartial to all the different social groups. If there was a character that stole my heart it was Mischief – Auraya’s pet veez – he added a much needed humour in the darkest times.<br /><br /><br />I can’t wait to see where this story goes next. The thing I love most about Trudi Canavan is her novels never disappoint. Great epic fantasy at its best.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17965708981223716110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I read it rather a short time after the Magicians Guild books - and so it took me a bit by surprise how different it was.<br/>While the first series is published as YA (here in Germany), the second series definitely is not. There is a bit of a love plot and some sex scenes in it - and of course the main protagonists are older.<br/>After I got used to the change - I did definitely enjoy the book, though it didn't completely blow me away.   <span id="freeText12255059079494059831" style="display:none">This one... I read it rather a short time after the Magicians Guild books - and so it took me a bit by surprise how different it was.<br />While the first series is published as YA (here in Germany), the second series definitely is not. There is a bit of a love plot and some sex scenes in it - and of course the main protagonists are older.<br />After I got used to the change - I did definitely enjoy the book, though it didn't completely blow me away. I liked the main character and definitely wanted to spend some more time with her in this new world. The pace was fast again, and the prose fluent as with her other books, but the story lacked a bit for me. I would have liked it a bit more - complex maybe? Can't really put my finger on it. <div id="review_2330422875" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2330422875" />
    <a title="Sky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40314361-sky"><img alt="Sky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522801708p2/40314361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2330422875?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sky" href="/user/show/40314361-sky">Sky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40314361-sky?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40314361-sky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40314361-sky?shelf=from-the-library">from-the-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2330422875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7581576264088518082">I <b>love</b> stories within fantasy that focus heavily on gods, priests, religions etc. so this grabbed my interest as soon as I saw it and it did not disappoint.<br/> <br/>I love multiple POV in books so I’m very pleased you usually get 2 or 3 POV’s in a chapter and it was not overwhelming either: you are given enough time to get to know a few characters before a new POV is added. There are a lot of characters but that is part of why I enjoyed it so much. <br/><br/>The world building is fantastic. Canavan created such a</span>
  <span id="freeText7581576264088518082" style="display:none">I <b>love</b> stories within fantasy that focus heavily on gods, priests, religions etc. so this grabbed my interest as soon as I saw it and it did not disappoint.<br /> <br />I love multiple POV in books so I’m very pleased you usually get 2 or 3 POV’s in a chapter and it was not overwhelming either: you are given enough time to get to know a few characters before a new POV is added. There are a lot of characters but that is part of why I enjoyed it so much. <br /><br />The world building is fantastic. Canavan created such a vibrant world with really rich cultures and races. There are a few different religions that are a major feature in this book and they are very well done. Canavan has also introduced us to two non-human societies in this novel and they are both unique takes on ideas that are not seen much in fantasy. <br /><br />I am so invested in Auraya, and also many of the other characters. The character growth is a strong point of the book for me as not only Auraya grows for both good and possibly bad but so do others and the possible outcomes of this growth are intriguing and I’m excited to read the next instalment to see where these characters will go next. <br /><br />There was also a bit of romance in this book which I personally enjoy and <b>I did not see it coming at all! </b> I think the mini-conclusion to the romance was well written: it feels wrapped up in this book but you still know there is more to it.<br /> <br />Something I really appreciate is that the story was actually wrapped up. Sometimes series have a tendency to leave you on a big cliff hanger just before a big reveal and I find it annoying. Canavan wrapped up this story very well but there are plenty of questions I still want answered.<br /> <br />Overall I really loved this story: it spoke to a lot of my personal preferences and had a strong execution. I am so excited to read the next book, just have to wait for my library hold to come in!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7581576264088518082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8425310430810491815">3.5 stars<br/><br/>In a world where magic and gods exist, Auraya has become one of the legendary, immortal 'Whites' - people chosen by the Gods to be their voices, and granted magical gifts and immortality. But Auraya doesn't have long to get used to her new position as Black Sorcerers from a neighboring land are intent on invading her world and killing those who impose them. <br/><br/>I enjoyed the quality of the writing in this, the care taken to unveil each character we follow and their personality and thought p</span>
  <span id="freeText8425310430810491815" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />In a world where magic and gods exist, Auraya has become one of the legendary, immortal 'Whites' - people chosen by the Gods to be their voices, and granted magical gifts and immortality. But Auraya doesn't have long to get used to her new position as Black Sorcerers from a neighboring land are intent on invading her world and killing those who impose them. <br /><br />I enjoyed the quality of the writing in this, the care taken to unveil each character we follow and their personality and thought processes and the magic and wonder in this world that Trudi Canavan created. I can see a lot of the same style of writing and imagination as I adored in The Black Magicians trilogy though unfortunately the slower pace of story didn't capture me quite as much.<br /><br />I felt this story quite slow, and there were times when I could describe myself as slightly bored. I was never rearing to get back to the book and pick it up which isn't a great sign. But this book is a real 'introduction' book to the world, the magic and the complex relationships between the different types of magic users as well as references to the history between them and occasionally resurfaces. I truly appreciate Trudi Canavan's slower, more expansive fantasy writing style and there were times in this book were I did feel anxious - such as during the big battle.<br /><br />I also really appreciate all the different creatures and types of races in this book from the Siyee to the Elai as well as adorable dog-like creatures like Mischief the veez (I need one so bad as a pet!).<br /><br />While this book didn't rock my socks off, I still enjoyed it and will be eager to pick up the rest of the series. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2254816699" />
    <a title="Eleanor (bookishcourtier)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64826682-eleanor-bookishcourtier"><img alt="Eleanor (bookishcourtier)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530384550p2/64826682.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eleanor (bookishcourtier)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eleanor (bookishcourtier)" href="/user/show/64826682-eleanor-bookishcourtier">Eleanor (bookishcourtier)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781841493862" href="/book/show/1017498.Priestess_of_the_White">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64826682-eleanor-bookishcourtier?shelf=two-star">two-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64826682-eleanor-bookishcourtier?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2254816699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12708202953322283638">2.5 stars<br/><br/><b> Sooo, while there were some things I liked about this book, it was just too slow and long and unexciting to merit anything higher than a 2 star rating. </b> I mean, I didn't hate it. That's why I upped my rating to 2.5 stars, because this was a pretty average book. There was nothing I loved, yet there was nothing that I though really problematic. <br/><br/><b> So, the world building wasn't amazing. </b> Trudi Canavan managed to convey the actual geography of the land itself to me, with the help of a map (t</span>
  <span id="freeText12708202953322283638" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br /><b> Sooo, while there were some things I liked about this book, it was just too slow and long and unexciting to merit anything higher than a 2 star rating. </b> I mean, I didn't hate it. That's why I upped my rating to 2.5 stars, because this was a pretty average book. There was nothing I loved, yet there was nothing that I though really problematic. <br /><br /><b> So, the world building wasn't amazing. </b> Trudi Canavan managed to convey the actual geography of the land itself to me, with the help of a map (thank goodness), which is made up of a load of Kingdoms that I can't remember the names of. But I seriously know nothing about these kingdoms - what is their culture? Their language? We literally never saw anything about them because the White (imaginative name, I know) are so elevated above them. I am also slightly confused about what the White rule. They seem revered everywhere, but they only seem to rule one kingdom? And they had to make all these alliances? For a war which didn't really have any causes? Things seemed to happen very conveniently so the plot could progress, especially at the end. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The gods are all like "no don't kill them it will create another war shh we won't tell you anything else" and this is just so "convenient". And there was this massive climax to a battle which didn't even last very long!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And I have no idea how magic is distributed and who gets it. <b> Also, most of the characters are very flat. </b> We have Auraya, the God's chosen, very good, wise etc. She had no depth. All the male characters seemed the same as well, and the only interesting character was Emerahl, and even she fell into some clichés later in the book. <b> I am also slightly concerned about the relationship between Auraya and Leiard. </b> She is 26, and he says he's forty, but he's not sure??!! And he was her teacher when she was 16. And he has white hair...so i pictured him as old. And even without this age gap, I was still not feeling the romance. It was just so...sudden. <br /><br /><b> I did like the Siyee though. </b> Triste was annoying, but I liked Drilli, and their romance was pretty cute. I think they were the most original part of the book - you don't read about many winged (as in, their arms are actually wings) tiny childlike creatures (not in any books I have read, anyway). <b> And I enjoyed Emerahl's point of view, as she was the most interesting character. </b> She was a bit less good than the others, and I think that made her more realistic. <br /><br /><b> This was just a bit to long and slow and flat for me. </b> I did consider reading the sequel but they are such long books and I really don't think I would make it. This had some promise but the world was pretty boring, and I just really didn't care about many of the characters. There were small things I liked about this, but the general overview of the book was just average. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12708202953322283638" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4804070757089419667">Interesting and with the potential to be better<br/><br/>The Good<br/>-------------------------------<br/>Secondary/Tertiary Characters: Most of the secondary viewpoint characters have some personality that make the story worth reading and some of the tertiary characters are good too. Character development is lacking for most characters though. Looking forward to more from the Hag.<br/><br/>Hints: There are many hints at history and future of the world -- enough potential to make continuing the series worth while.<br/><br/>The Bad<br/>----</span>
  <span id="freeText4804070757089419667" style="display:none">Interesting and with the potential to be better<br /><br />The Good<br />-------------------------------<br />Secondary/Tertiary Characters: Most of the secondary viewpoint characters have some personality that make the story worth reading and some of the tertiary characters are good too. Character development is lacking for most characters though. Looking forward to more from the Hag.<br /><br />Hints: There are many hints at history and future of the world -- enough potential to make continuing the series worth while.<br /><br />The Bad<br />-------------------------------<br />World Building: I don't find the world all that interesting. Canavan's need to have fantasy names for all plants, animals, and beverages make the world less comprehensible (one of the annoyances of using an ebook is the glossary is not as accessible). While the area of the Si is more compelling, the rest of the world is pretty generic.<br /><br />Auraya: a clone of Sonea of the Black Magician trilogy -- too good, smart, perceptive, etc. She just doesn't come across as a real person.<br /><br />Story arc: Honestly there are no surprises in the story. The main story arc plods forward with no deviation or real turmoil (even with a war). There are a few developments, but no panic, suspense, or serious drama.<br /><br /><br />Hoping for more in the second book!</span>

<div id="review_1058113350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1058113350?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dakota★Magic in Every Book" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dakota★Magic in Every Book" href="/user/show/25489228-dakota-magic-in-every-book">Dakota★Magic in Every Book</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25489228-dakota-magic-in-every-book?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25489228-dakota-magic-in-every-book?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1058113350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11147030747096584214"><b>First Read, 2014</b><br/>While a tad slow and scattered at the beginning, I was thoroughly involved and enjoying the story as I read further on. Despite criticisms I've read of this series, I find Priestess of the White a strong beginning to a high fantasy trilogy with interesting races, animals, magic, and Gods.<br/><br/><b>Second Read, 2015</b><br/>	After reading this book a second time, I really can't figure out why I only gave this book four stars the first time. While this book can be slow, filled with world-building inf</span>
  <span id="freeText11147030747096584214" style="display:none"><b>First Read, 2014</b><br />While a tad slow and scattered at the beginning, I was thoroughly involved and enjoying the story as I read further on. Despite criticisms I've read of this series, I find Priestess of the White a strong beginning to a high fantasy trilogy with interesting races, animals, magic, and Gods.<br /><br /><b>Second Read, 2015</b><br />	After reading this book a second time, I really can't figure out why I only gave this book four stars the first time. While this book can be slow, filled with world-building information, and a bit confusing at first with the rotating third person perspective, I think it's honestly a very solid and impressive first book for a high fantasy trilogy. There's a lot of very well-done and thought out world building, including interesting races (that aren't elves and dwarves), history, culture, a unique portrayal of magic, and also an interesting examination of gods, religion, and belief. As much as it saddens me to seen negative reviews, I do understand the slow world building and pacing aren't for everyone. Still, it's a very well done first book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11147030747096584214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17878620-margaretdh?shelf=not-everything-you-d-hope-for">not-everything-you-d-hope-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17878620-margaretdh?shelf=other-worlds">other-worlds</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17878620-margaretdh?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17878620-margaretdh?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17878620-margaretdh?shelf=chips-and-chocolate-bars">chips-and-chocolate-bars</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2148629890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17457862985370843837">This wasn't actively terrible, but it wasn't great. The writing and world building are both pretty pedestrian, and the plot is an old standard. The characters are all pretty one dimensional with fairly straightforward conflicts, and fantasy names that made me, a person who has a pretty high tolerance for made up stuff, roll my eyes.<br/><br/>Before I had access to the book-ternet, I might have liked this book. I've always had a soft spot for fantasy and good guy vs. bad guy show downs, and this would prob</span>
  <span id="freeText17457862985370843837" style="display:none">This wasn't actively terrible, but it wasn't great. The writing and world building are both pretty pedestrian, and the plot is an old standard. The characters are all pretty one dimensional with fairly straightforward conflicts, and fantasy names that made me, a person who has a pretty high tolerance for made up stuff, roll my eyes.<br /><br />Before I had access to the book-ternet, I might have liked this book. I've always had a soft spot for fantasy and good guy vs. bad guy show downs, and this would probably have scratched an itch. But now that I've got some tools for finding books that a better written and more inventive, this was pretty blah.<br /><br /> I wouldn't recommend it, and if you're looking for some accessible fantasy to lose yourself in, I'd suggest someone like David Eddings. He's not going to blow your doors off, but if you're looking for epic fantasy that doesn't ask too much of you, his world building and characterization is more inventive, and he jazzes up the old plot standards more effectively.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17457862985370843837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3847545353644527454">Was looking for a new author (having exhausted all the ones I know I like). Ran across this in the local library. I really couldn't get into it. The writing was a bit clunky and the plotline seemed fairly standard high fantasy by the time I gave up. The world building seemed potentially interesting, but I couldn't bring myself to care enough to keep reading. I gather from other comments that this author has more interesting works, so I may try another book another time.</span>

<div id="review_2810184252" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2810184252" />
    <a title="Jessica Eck" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63040194-jessica-eck"><img alt="Jessica Eck" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482785660p2/63040194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2810184252?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Eck" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Eck" href="/user/show/63040194-jessica-eck">Jessica Eck</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2810184252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9081293057906862891">Several years ago I read the "Black Magician" trilogy by Trudi Canavan and right afterwards I read the first two books of "Age of the Five". Despite enjoying them, I never read the last book for some reason.<br/><br/>By accident I found the audio books on audible and decided to give the series another try and I don't regret it so far! As I didn't remember much of what happened in the first two books, I decided to start with them.<br/><br/>Sarah Douglas' reading is very enjoyable and I especially love how she reads </span>
  <span id="freeText9081293057906862891" style="display:none">Several years ago I read the "Black Magician" trilogy by Trudi Canavan and right afterwards I read the first two books of "Age of the Five". Despite enjoying them, I never read the last book for some reason.<br /><br />By accident I found the audio books on audible and decided to give the series another try and I don't regret it so far! As I didn't remember much of what happened in the first two books, I decided to start with them.<br /><br />Sarah Douglas' reading is very enjoyable and I especially love how she reads Mischief (Auraya's talking pet and easily my favourite character). <br /><br />There are quiet a few characters (which I like in fantasy books) and most of them are interesting or at least likeable. Auraya unfortunately only belongs to the "likeable". I like her, but she isn't really interesting. Leiard and Mirar, however, are, and I can't wait to see what happens with them. I also can't wait to find out more about the other Whites, especially Juran, and their gods. <br /><br />The world and the magic system are both well-done and we don't just get to read about several different human cultures, but also other races, like the Siyee, a small race with wings. <br /><br />I really enjoyed "Priestess of the White" and I'm sure that this time I will finish the series :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="9081293057906862891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/17410148-priestess-of-the-white">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2713024415&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2713024415" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3116844828837156730">I listened to this book on Audible.<br/><br/>I have been uhmming and ahhing about if this was 2 stars or 3 stars and I've finally settled on 2. I will try and explain why.<br/><br/>I enjoyed parts of this book and became invested in Emerahl's side, however, she was mostly a side character. I enjoyed some interesting plot points, in particular, the Siyee Tryss and again everything about Emerahl (and Mirah).<br/><br/>The problem here lies with Auraya, the main character. Her personality consists of being attracted to an older </span>
  <span id="freeText3116844828837156730" style="display:none">I listened to this book on Audible.<br /><br />I have been uhmming and ahhing about if this was 2 stars or 3 stars and I've finally settled on 2. I will try and explain why.<br /><br />I enjoyed parts of this book and became invested in Emerahl's side, however, she was mostly a side character. I enjoyed some interesting plot points, in particular, the Siyee Tryss and again everything about Emerahl (and Mirah).<br /><br />The problem here lies with Auraya, the main character. Her personality consists of being attracted to an older man which is problematic due to clashing faiths. And that she's not a massive racist. That's... that's not a personality. <br /><br />Also, does Canavan have a thing for older men? I love The Magician's Guild, but I really didn't need a recurring theme. Also, can't we switch a trope up? Make her older? <br /><br />Additionally, and coming from a Brandon Sanderson fan, I felt the book was too long. And in an intensely linear way. So instead of getting lost in the woods, you were walking down a very straight and boring road. It felt like a tick list of things had to be checked off before the war started - very convenient! Nice how the army waited until all alliances were tied up before attacking. There was no sense of urgency or danger. Even when the fighting started I was like 'oh okay so there is actually a war. Everyone is super calm about this'.<br /><br />Anyway, slow, unexciting book with an anticlimax and a female character with less personality than battered pair of sweatpants - it landed on the bad side.<br /><br />I also know exactly where the trilogy is going. <br /><br />I want to see how my faves deal with the impending revelations, so maybe I'll try this as a book (so I can skip Auraya or something) and when it's 99p. <br /><br />Got to be honest, as a Trudi Canavan fan, I was disappointed. Nevermind!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3116844828837156730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8229490-priestess-of-the-white">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8541930-elisabeth-cook?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8541930-elisabeth-cook?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8541930-elisabeth-cook?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1036975466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6748935792193541790">I <b>love</b> the Black Magicians Trilogy, so it pains me to review another Trudi Canavan book with a DNF at 66%. I like the concept of <i>Priestess</i>, the fragile balance between magic and the power of the gods is quite an original feeling backdrop (to me). Unfortunately, there are too many disappointments elsewhere. After the hundreds of pages I've read, I still don't have much of a sense of the protagonist, Auraya's personality; I don't know what motivates her, what she finds funny, or what distinguishes</span>
  <span id="freeText6748935792193541790" style="display:none">I <b>love</b> the Black Magicians Trilogy, so it pains me to review another Trudi Canavan book with a DNF at 66%. I like the concept of <i>Priestess</i>, the fragile balance between magic and the power of the gods is quite an original feeling backdrop (to me). Unfortunately, there are too many disappointments elsewhere. After the hundreds of pages I've read, I still don't have much of a sense of the protagonist, Auraya's personality; I don't know what motivates her, what she finds funny, or what distinguishes her from the (also two-dimensional) characters she interacts with. I did, however, enjoy reading the story of Emerahl and her character alone might motivate me to finish this book in the future, but the plot going on around her is slow and uninteresting. Finally, I was pretty disappointed by how familiar it all felt: a young woman taken to be trained as a magician, but whose ideas about the world differ from the institution; the threat of stronger foreign magicians across the border; <b>SPOILER</b> love interest with a once-teacher - it felt all too much like a rehash of Sonea and Kyralia. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6748935792193541790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47769167" />
    <a title="Maria Elmvang" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/168347-maria-elmvang"><img alt="Maria Elmvang" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442612167p2/168347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780732278694" href="/book/show/4040841-priestess-of-the-white">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/168347-maria-elmvang?shelf=owned-physical-book">owned-physical-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/168347-maria-elmvang?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/168347-maria-elmvang?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/168347-maria-elmvang?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/168347-maria-elmvang?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47769167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11192338859434385223">I was a bit disappointed by this book at first. I had LOVED <u>The Black Magician</u> trilogy, and was sad to see that this book couldn't quite live up to the first in that series. It was obviously aimed at a younger audience (at least the beginning was - it did get significantly darker near the end) and the characters didn't seem nearly as complex. Still, it was good enough to keep me entertained through all 672 pages and I would in no way "dis-recommend" it... I'd just tell people to read the other t</span>
  <span id="freeText11192338859434385223" style="display:none">I was a bit disappointed by this book at first. I had LOVED <u>The Black Magician</u> trilogy, and was sad to see that this book couldn't quite live up to the first in that series. It was obviously aimed at a younger audience (at least the beginning was - it did get significantly darker near the end) and the characters didn't seem nearly as complex. Still, it was good enough to keep me entertained through all 672 pages and I would in no way "dis-recommend" it... I'd just tell people to read the other trilogy instead, if they hadn't already.<br /><br />Like in "Black Magician" Trudi Canavan manages to keep track of an impressively large number of characters, and though the focus keeps shifting from one to the other, she keeps all plot lines equally interesting, so that one doesn't mind abandoning one major character for another. Usually I prefer sticking to just one or two viewpoints, but it actually worked really well here. I was especially fascinated by the people of Si and Elai and hope we get to hear more about the latter in later books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11192338859434385223" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_349697049" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/349697049" />
    <a title="Rowena Tylden-Pattenson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7233110-rowena-tylden-pattenson"><img alt="Rowena Tylden-Pattenson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450216267p2/7233110.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/349697049?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rowena Tylden-Pattenson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rowena Tylden-Pattenson" href="/user/show/7233110-rowena-tylden-pattenson">Rowena Tylden-Pattenson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781841493862" href="/book/show/1017498.Priestess_of_the_White">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7233110-rowena-tylden-pattenson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349697049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12978708487216110048">I hold Trudi Canavan's books to high expectation, because she's produced some very fine novels over the course of her career. This one though, I know is one of her earlier novels, so I wasn't expecting quite as much from it- and there is evidence that she hasn't quite developed her style and characters completely in this one. I enjoyed it, but I don't think I'd recommend it as one of my favourites.<br/><br/>The plot was interesting enough, if not fairly common; two warring countries, magic, sorcerers etc.</span>
  <span id="freeText12978708487216110048" style="display:none">I hold Trudi Canavan's books to high expectation, because she's produced some very fine novels over the course of her career. This one though, I know is one of her earlier novels, so I wasn't expecting quite as much from it- and there is evidence that she hasn't quite developed her style and characters completely in this one. I enjoyed it, but I don't think I'd recommend it as one of my favourites.<br /><br />The plot was interesting enough, if not fairly common; two warring countries, magic, sorcerers etc. etc. Fairly standard stuff, although told well. There's a large cast of characters, some only briefly appearing for a chapter- perhaps to add in the viewpoint of a 'normal' citizen? Although it seems a little trite and most of these sections could have been told in a different way. <br /><br />The characters were okay, but lacked strong personalities. Emerahl was by far both the most interesting and the most developed, and definitely the character I looked forward to the chapters of most. I think if it came to warring between Emerahl and the White in later books, she'd be the one I'll be rooting for, regardless of Auraya posing as the main protagonist. She was very bland and I didn't really relate, as she seemed to have little personality; as did the other Whites. <br /><br />Good enough stock fantasy, but nothing special.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12978708487216110048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2798959901" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2798959901" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63425021-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2798959901?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/63425021-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781841493862" href="/book/show/1017498.Priestess_of_the_White">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2798959901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1891209732159270653">I love this book, it ticks all of my boxes. The powerful flying immortal sorceress, the thoughtful use of magic, high stakes and people you care about. I am also fascinated by the thought experiment the book - and the trilogy - embodies: what if there could be no doubt that gods were real, and powerful? How does that change what religion is, and how it plays out in a society? If serving the gods grants power, and immortality, does that change the motivations of their followers? <br/><br/>I also love the w</span>
  <span id="freeText1891209732159270653" style="display:none">I love this book, it ticks all of my boxes. The powerful flying immortal sorceress, the thoughtful use of magic, high stakes and people you care about. I am also fascinated by the thought experiment the book - and the trilogy - embodies: what if there could be no doubt that gods were real, and powerful? How does that change what religion is, and how it plays out in a society? If serving the gods grants power, and immortality, does that change the motivations of their followers? <br /><br />I also love the world, particularly the use of magic and the Siyee and Elai peoples, created to be human adaptations for the sky and the water respectively. It's one of those places that now lives in my imagination, with Wonderland and Narnia.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1891209732159270653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2545375454" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2545375454" />
    <a title="Der blaue Buchling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39167013-der-blaue-buchling"><img alt="Der blaue Buchling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498684787p2/39167013.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2545375454?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Der blaue Buchling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Der blaue Buchling" href="/user/show/39167013-der-blaue-buchling">Der blaue Buchling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841499635" href="/book/show/20997850-priestess-of-the-white">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2545375454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3408438275602441048">The thing is: it’s not a bad read, and I thought it fairly comfortable and quick to read. There were a few characters I liked, for example Emerahl and Tryss, and the strongest point is probably the worldbuilding. But - it felt in several parts rushed and most of the characters are a little bland. It’s enjoyable, but I don’t need to read the next part as soon as possible or else I’ll die from suspension. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ueMBesAzth4xJj3Nx5OW0OmtEb3jY3lZkR/F5xC+l+UrpDA1d7okcQoDii3GMvYREiyGvKjnTxa0PxHSgeiobg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('esbcXw6HPbHgY5lNtrKKm0jBenO52zvUDPShaje7pjzoge0QuQ6v3ttGLq23E+pas0DtcvJfDZsp1HVfpu2Ztw==')})
  }

Nawiązuje do współczesności, odsłaniając kulisy obejmowania władzy w Polsce przez prawicę. Tropi polskiego łącznika Al-Kaidy oraz pokazuje metody działania szwedzkich służb specjalnych.\n\nBohaterami powieści są tzw. nielegałowie, supertajni szpiedzy posługujący się za granicą nową tożsamością i dorobioną &quot;legendą&quot;.\n\nKonrad powraca do Warszawy po zakończonej fiaskiem misji na Bliskim Wschodzie: znów nie udało mu się dopaść „Karola” vel Safira as-Salama, polskiego odszczepieńca, łącznika Al-Kaidy... Niejaki Hans Jorgensen szuka w szwedzkiej prasie niewinnych na pozór ogłoszeń, z których następnie odszyfrowuje zakodowane informacje... Pułkownik Stiepanowycz z mińskiego KGB krótko cieszy się z zarobionych na przemycie dolarów, gdyż pada ofiarą napadu... W październiku 1939 roku w Moskwie Beria, naczelnik NKWD, słucha referatu majora Zarubina na temat działań wywiadowczo-operacyjnych na terenie Polski. W gabinecie prezesa IPN zjawia się profesor Barda i twierdzi, że ma dokumenty, które rzucają całkiem nowe światło na zbrodnię katyńską... We współczesnej Polsce stanowisko prezydenta piastuje Stanisław Zieliński, lecz rzeczywista władza spoczywa w rękach szefa jego kancelarii, Marcina Kamińskiego – osobnika o niezbyt reprezentacyjnej aparycji, za to cieszącego się poparciem konserwatywnego elektoratu.\n\nWszystkie te na pierwszy rzut oka odległe od siebie wątki, postacie, miejsca i wydarzenia łączą się w niezwykłą, precyzyjnie <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9434412017321459525">Trudi Canavan was born in Kew, Melbourne and grew up in Ferntree Gully, a suburb at the foothills of the Dandenongs.<br/><br/>In 1999 she won the Aurealis Award for Best Fantasy Short Story with “Whispers of the Mist Children”. In the same year she was granted a writers residency at Varuna Writers’ Centre in Katoomba, New South Wales.<br/><br/>In November 2001, The Magicians’ Guild was first published in Australia. T</span>
  <span id="freeText9434412017321459525" style="display:none">Trudi Canavan was born in Kew, Melbourne and grew up in Ferntree Gully, a suburb at the foothills of the Dandenongs.<br /><br />In 1999 she won the Aurealis Award for Best Fantasy Short Story with “Whispers of the Mist Children”. In the same year she was granted a writers residency at Varuna Writers’ Centre in Katoomba, New South Wales.<br /><br />In November 2001, The Magicians’ Guild was first published in Australia. The second book of the trilogy, The Novice, was published in June 2002 and was nominated for the Aurealis Award for Best Fantasy Novel. The third book The High Lord was released in January 2003 and was nominated for the Best Novel Ditmar category. All three books entered Australian top ten SF bestseller lists.<br /><br />The Black Magician Trilogy reached the international market in 2004, published by HarperCollins’ EOS imprint in North America and Orbit Books in the UK. The trilogy is now rated by Nielsen BookScan as the most successful debut fantasy series of the last 10 years.<br /><br />Trudi’s second trilogy, Age of the Five, has also enjoyed bestselling success. Priestess of the White reached No.3 in the Sunday Times hardback fiction bestseller list, staying in the top ten for six weeks.<br /><br />In early 2006 Trudi signed a seven-figure contract with Orbit to write the prequel and sequel to the Black Magician Trilogy. The prequel, The Magician’s Apprentice was released in 2009 and won the Best Fantasy Novel category of the Aurealis Awards. She is now working on the sequel trilogy, and planning her next fantasy series, which will be set in an entirely new world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9434412017321459525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
